Youth Association Municipal Lecture 104

An Overview of the Shanghai International Settlement Municipality

The Shanghai Youth Association held a municipal lecture the day before yesterday titled "An Overview of the Shanghai International Settlement Municipality." The speaker was Mr. He Dekui, secretary of the Chinese Ratepayers' Association. The following is a record of his speech:

(1) The origin of the International Settlement dates back to 1842, when China and Britain signed the Treaty of Nanjing, stipulating that Guangzhou, Xiamen, Fuzhou, Ningbo, and Shanghai be opened as treaty ports for trade. The following year, Shanghai was designated as a place for foreign merchants to trade, allowing British residents to live north of the Yangjingbang Creek. However, Chinese government officials were not allowed to sell land outright to the British, only to grant them perpetual lease rights. This is where the name "settlement" comes from. Later, other countries also signed trade treaties with the Qing government. Consequently, there were also people from other countries living in the British settlement, including American missionaries and merchants. Some even acquired property and resided in Hongkou, thus forming the so-called American Settlement. The areas of the British and American settlements gradually expanded as the population grew. In 1863, the British and American settlements merged to form the International Settlement. This is a general overview of the origin of the International Settlement.

(2) The current situation of mixed Chinese and foreign residence in the International Settlement: Before 1899, the area of the International Settlement was 10,006 mu. The current area of the International Settlement was expanded in 1899 with the approval of the Shanghai Daotai, increasing it by more than three times the original area, totaling 33,503 mu. According to the population statistics of last October, residents of the International Settlement came from 47 countries. Among them, foreign men, women, and children totaled more than 36,400, with Japanese being the largest group at more than 18,400. The British were the second largest with more than 6,200, followed by Russians with more than 3,400. Indians, Americans, and Portuguese followed, each with more than 1,000. The Chinese residing in the International Settlement, including men, women, and children, totaled more than 971,000, with Jiangsu natives accounting for the largest number at 500,000, followed by Zhejiang natives with 300,000, Guangdong natives with more than 44,000, and Anhui natives with more than 20,000, ranking fourth. This is a general overview of the area and population of the International Settlement.

(3) The autonomous system of the International Settlement: The municipality of the International Settlement is a local autonomous system, with the Land Regulations as its basic law and foundation for autonomy. According to the provisions of these Land Regulations, municipal power belongs to the ratepayers. Any foreigner within the settlement who owns property used for business purposes with a value of 500 taels, and who pays annual property or land or land and building taxes of more than 10 taels in addition to the license fee, or who rents a house with an annual rent of more than 500 taels and pays taxes, is qualified as a ratepayer, has the right to elect members of the Shanghai Municipal Council (SMC), and may attend the ratepayers' meeting. As for foreigners inside or outside the settlement who pay land taxes of more than 50 taels annually in addition to the license fee, or who rent a house with an annual rent of more than 1,200 taels and pay taxes, they are not only able to attend the ratepayers' meeting and have the right to vote, but also have the qualifications to be elected as members of the SMC. According to the Land Regulations, the foreign members of the SMC must be at least five and no more than nine. Each year, the consuls of various countries stationed in Shanghai convene an annual meeting of foreign ratepayers in February or March to elect members and to deliberate on all important matters of the SMC, review the SMC's financial statements for the previous year, and deliberate on the budget for the current year. There is no quorum for this annual meeting, and it can be held regardless of the number of attendees. However, all motions are still decided by a majority of those present. In case of special issues concerning the settlement, one or more consuls may convene, or 25 ratepayers may jointly request, a special meeting of foreign ratepayers. This special meeting requires the attendance of one-third of the foreign ratepayers to be convened, and motions are still decided by a majority of those present. The SMC members must prepare a report on the municipal situation in the past year, and must submit the financial statements for the previous year and the budget for the current year to the ratepayers' annual meeting. There are about 2,700 foreign ratepayers inside and outside the settlement, but the number of attendees at the annual meeting is not large. The proposals put forward by the SMC are usually passed. This is a general overview of the autonomous system of the International Settlement.

(4) The relationship between Chinese ratepayers and the municipal affairs of the settlement: Since 1926, the Chinese Ratepayers' Association has been able to nominate three Chinese members to join the SMC and participate in the municipal affairs of the settlement. Although this is not stipulated in the Land Regulations, it was negotiated and agreed upon by the Consular Body and the Chinese authorities. The first time three Chinese members joined the SMC was in 1928. Until 1930, the number of Western members remained at nine, while the number of Chinese members increased to five. This was also decided after consultation between the Consular Body and the Chinese authorities. The qualifications of Chinese ratepayers and their qualifications to be elected as Chinese members are exactly the same as those of foreign ratepayers and foreign members mentioned above. However, foreign members do not have to reside in Shanghai for more than five years, while according to the regulations of the Chinese Ratepayers' Association, all Chinese members must reside in the settlement for more than five years. This is the only difference.

(5) The organization of the SMC and its committees: At present, the SMC has a total of fourteen members. In addition to the five Chinese members, there are usually five British members, two American members, and two Japanese members. The important administration of the SMC is decided by the SMC, and the SMC also has the power to appoint or dismiss personnel working in the bureau. SMC meetings are held once every two or three weeks. Usually, if there are important official documents, they are sent to each member for their comments. The SMC has one chairman and one vice-chairman, who are elected from among the members. All members are honorary positions and are not paid. However, because there are many matters to be decided by the SMC, and they are very complex in nature, various committees are set up in addition to the SMC, such as the Police Committee, Finance Committee, Works Committee, Health Committee, Education Committee, Staff Committee, Traffic Committee, Public Utilities Committee, Music Committee, Library Committee, and Public Sports Ground Committee. The number of people on these committees ranges from two or three to seven or eight. For more important committees, there must be one or two SMC members on the committee. If a problem occurs in the SMC, it is usually first discussed by the relevant committee, and a resolution is made, which is then reviewed by the SMC. It is only valid after approval by the SMC. These committees discuss their respective affairs separately and must obtain the approval of the SMC, so the procedures are more complete. Most of these committees are honorary positions, except for one or two that are paid. When the Chinese Ratepayers' Association nominated three Chinese members to join the SMC in 1928, they also nominated six Chinese committee members to join the various committees of the SMC. In recent years, the SMC has often had special problems, and has established several new committees and invited more Chinese committee members to join. Therefore, the total number of Chinese committee members in the various committees of the SMC is now more than ten. Because the SMC and various committees are all honorary positions, and because each member and committee member is engaged in business, they can only take care of more important issues and can only decide on policies, so the SMC often employs paid civil servants to carry out affairs according to the policies they have set.

(6) The permanent organs of the SMC: The various executive powers of the SMC are all in the hands of the permanently employed and paid civil servants. The highest position among the paid personnel was originally called Director General, but from April 1st of this year, the name was changed to Secretary General, translated as "督辦" (supervisor). Below him are 总办 (General Manager), Secretary, as well as the Chief of Police, Chief of Finance, Chief of Works, Chief of Health, Chief of Education, Chief of Taxes, Municipal Advocate, Fire Chief, and Commander of the Shanghai Volunteer Corps, who are in charge of various administrative matters. The above-mentioned departments have many employees and require a lot of expenses. The SMC's budget for 1930 was 16 million taels for the whole year, of which the Police Department accounted for more than 5.4 million taels, the Works Department accounted for more than 3.7 million taels, the Health Department accounted for more than 800,000 taels, the General Affairs Department accounted for 590,000 taels, and the Finance Department also accounted for more than 270,000 taels. These are all important organs of the SMC. The General Affairs Department is so named because all external announcements of the SMC must be announced through the General Affairs Department.

(7) The minimum expectations for the SMC: According to a survey in 1930, the residents of the International Settlement, all foreigners combined, account for only slightly more than 3% of the total number of residents, and the rest are Chinese. The property and taxes paid by the Chinese in the settlement also account for more than half. Therefore, the impact of the administration and all measures of the settlement on the Chinese is naturally greater than that on foreigners. The administration of our settlement has always been biased towards foreigners. All senior administrative personnel are foreigners. The positions of Chinese are always lower than those of foreign personnel, and they have no real power in their hands. Because of differences in customs, habits, language, etc., the Chinese and foreigners are different, so all the measures of the senior administrative personnel of the SMC are often not suitable for the Chinese, causing various misunderstandings, or even leading to unfortunate incidents. At present, there are already Chinese members on the SMC and Chinese committee members on the various committees, which is a great improvement compared to the past. However, it is still a pity that there are not many Chinese employed in senior paid positions, so that they can do their best to assist in administrative affairs. Since the Chinese in the settlement account for more than 96% of the total population, more Chinese should be employed as senior paid personnel to increase the efficiency of administration, because seeking the welfare of the majority of Chinese residents in the settlement is seeking improvement in the municipal administration of the International Settlement. If senior administrative personnel can employ more Chinese, all measures in the International Settlement will be able to eliminate various barriers and work together in the spirit of Chinese-foreign cooperation to seek progress in the municipal administration of the settlement. There is nothing more important for the SMC to do at present. Recently, our countrymen have had persistent demands regarding the concessions of various countries in China. During this transitional period, the settlement authorities should have a thorough understanding and a bright attitude. However, because this issue is slightly different from the scope of discussion of this topic, and because of the limited time, I cannot discuss it in detail. Therefore, I will only state the minimum expectations as above.

News of Price Increases for Yangtze River Steamers 106

The Customs Brokers' Association Opposes

The Taikoo Steam Navigation Company initiated a meeting with China Merchants Steam Navigation, Sanpei, Ningshao, and other companies to discuss cooperation and increase freight rates to avoid competition among the industry. The Hankou Customs Brokers' Association opposed this and submitted a request to the Ministry of Communications to stop it. After receiving the request, the Ministry of Communications ordered the Shanghai Shipping Association to investigate and respond. The Shipping Association then responded, stating that the six companies, including China Merchants Steam Navigation, had agreed on water freight rates according to the old practice to avoid competition and follow business customs. It was unavoidable and did not involve selling out Chinese merchants. The Ministry of Communications then approved the Hankou Customs Brokers' Association to be informed. According to Shi Zhikun, chairman of the Shanghai Customs Brokers' Association, the increase in water freight rates agreed upon by Taikoo, China Merchants Steam Navigation, Sanpei, and other companies is based on the example of last year. However, when the Yangtze River water freight rates of the various companies increased by 20% last year, it was stated that it would be based on the water level. This time, the agreed increase will be the same regardless of the water level. The details are currently being discussed, and it will be implemented as soon as it is agreed upon.

Shanghai South Public Bus Longhua Special Bus Security Team Police Provoke Trouble 110

Forcibly Occupy Vehicles and Force Departure from Shanghai

Assault Ticket Seller Ni Wuyi

The Shanghai South Public Bus Company, because of the beautiful spring weather and the opening of Longhua peach blossoms, added seven Route 2 buses on the first day of this month, specially to Longhua, for the convenience of visitors. Unexpectedly, at about 4:00 p.m. yesterday, Gao, the squad leader of the First Team stationed in Longhua of the Caohejing Security Team, led more than 20 policemen to forcibly occupy the vehicles without buying tickets, causing an argument and assaulting Ni Wuyi, the ticket seller of Bus No. 27, resulting in the complete shutdown of public buses, traffic interruption, and major chaos. The details are recorded as follows:

The Cause of the Trouble: The Route 2 buses specially put on by the Shanghai South Public Bus Company arrived at the last stop of Longhua Temple at 4:10 p.m. yesterday and were picking up tourists to return to Shanghai. Suddenly, Gao, the squad leader of the First Team stationed in Longhua of the Caohejing Security Team, led more than 20 policemen to board the bus. Because the weather was mild and it was Sunday, there were many tourists in Longhua who wanted to take the bus back to Shanghai. The policemen occupied the seats and refused to let the tourists board, saying that the bus was a chartered bus and no passengers were allowed. Seeing that they were armed policemen, the tourists did not argue with them to avoid trouble, and could only wait for the next bus to arrive. After the bus departed, the ticket seller Ni Wuyi asked them to buy half-price tickets because they were military and police personnel. Unexpectedly, they ignored him. The ticket seller, seeing that there were many of them, could not argue and allowed them to ride. When the bus traveled about a mile to Maogong Bridge Station, the policemen suddenly got off the bus all at once, leaving no one in the bus. The driver saw that there were many tourists at Longhua Temple Station and wanted to drive the empty bus back to Longhua to pick up more tourists. When the bus was turning around, the policemen ordered him to drive the empty bus back to Shanghai and not to drive to Longhua again. They dragged Ni Wuyi, the ticket seller of Bus No. 27, off the bus, beat him, and then dispersed. The ticket seller suffered serious injuries to his waist and legs. Traffic was interrupted. After this incident occurred, the driver immediately notified the company by telephone, detailing the assault. Yang Pingcai, the director of the business department, and Xia Shuxiang, the director of the vehicle department of the company, were furious when they heard about this. They immediately went to the scene of the incident in Longhua and sent the injured person and the bus to the hospital for treatment. At the same time, they ordered all 12 buses that were driving to Longhua to stop. Because there were so many tourists in Longhua yesterday who were waiting for the bus to return to Shanghai, the temporary traffic interruption caused major chaos, and the onlookers were packed like sardines.

Authorities Mediate: Because yesterday was Sunday, the Shanghai Public Security Bureau was afraid that the crowd in Longhua would cause trouble, so they ordered Gao, the chief of the Sixth District, Third Precinct, to lead the police to maintain order nearby. Zhang, the director of the Second Section of the Traffic Department of the Public Security Bureau, and An, the director of the Fourth Section of the Vehicle Department of the Public Utilities Bureau, were also playing in Longhua yesterday and had not returned. When Zhang and An heard about this, they consulted with Yang and Xia of the bus company, and asked them to restore bus traffic first and be responsible for solving everything. Yang and Xia, with the permission of the authorities and to avoid disturbing the public's transportation, resumed normal operation at about 5:00 p.m.

Old Man's Corpse Divided into Two Coffins 111

Autopsy Results Show Corpse Relocation

Some Say the Corpse is 300 Years Old

Ancient Coffin Dug Up in Xiaoximen

Selling the Coffin and Cutting the Corpse, Discarding it in an Open Space

The Shanghai District Court previously received a report from Gu Tiuyun, the Baotou of the 25th Bao, 12th Tu, stating that there were two small wooden coffins on the open space of the Jiangxi Guild Hall on South Railway Station Branch Road, containing the head and body of an old man, with two wooden boxes and white bones on top. The corpses in the coffins were not completely decayed, but were cut into two sections. Fearing that it was a murder, he requested an autopsy. The District Court sent Prosecutor Wang and Examiner Xuan to the scene. The autopsy revealed that it was a corpse relocation. However, the purpose of the relocation was probably to steal the burial objects. However, this kind of behavior violated the law. Therefore, Prosecutor Wang sent the police to cooperate with the Baotou to investigate who the corpse belonged to, who excavated it, and whether the burial objects were stolen, so as to arrest the murderer. However, according to the people nearby, an ancient coffin and other white bones were found when renovating houses in Xiaoximen. The ancient coffin was completely un-decayed, with the vermilion lacquer still bright. There must have been valuable items inside. It was opened, and there was an old man's corpse inside, with gray hair and beard. The clothes and skin had not changed. The clothing was still in the style of more than 300 years ago. It is said that the coffin was made of lead wood, so it did not change over time. Later, someone took the coffin away and sold it, and the corpse rotted. Then, they cut the corpse into sections and put it into small coffins and discarded it in an open space, so there are no family members, etc. However, because no one came forward to testify, it was not convenient to report and investigate.

Supervision Was Improper

What Exactly Happened?

Defiles His Wife and Beats Her Husband 124

Wang Kaizi's Lustful Courage Knows No Bounds

Shen Shunyuan, 30 years old, from Nanxiang, resides at No. 719 Huining Road. He works as a cook. His wife, Xie, 21 years old, went to a matchmaker shop on Sanjiao Street a month ago, entrusting them to introduce her to a job as a maid because she was concerned about the family's poverty. Unexpectedly, she was soon lured by a man named Wang Kaizi to a small inn near the Shanghai military camp for illicit cohabitation. Wang even cheated the woman out of her clothes and pawned them. Shen, after losing his wife, searched everywhere without a trace. He finally found her the day before yesterday, inquired about the events, and had no choice but to accept his misfortune. He went out with her to redeem her pawned clothes. Unexpectedly, Wang Kaizi learned about it and secretly gathered Wang A'san and others to ambush them on the way. They beat Shen recklessly. Shen shouted for help, and the watchman police, Sun Shaozhen, from the twenty-fifth post in the area, heard the sound and rushed over. Wang Kaizi had already escaped, and only Wang A'san was caught. They were taken back to the First Sub-station of the First District along with Shen and the woman for preliminary trial and handling.

Partnership Comprador's Money Dispute Lawsuit 125

Lu Jiupeng hired a lawyer to represent him and filed a lawsuit in the civil court of the French Concession, stating that the plaintiff and the defendant, Luo Yanfu, had formed a partnership as compradores in the American-owned Jinlong Tobacco Company. They agreed on a contract that all expenses would be paid by the plaintiff. Subsequently, the plaintiff successively paid more than 24,503 dollars. After repaying 5,000 dollars, more than 19,000 dollars were still owed. Later, due to the lack of goods to sell, the partnership agreement was cancelled. The defendant issued a promissory note with a limited time for repayment, guaranteed by Chen Zuming and Guanhua Hat Shop. However, the hat shop has closed down, and Chen has disappeared. The court was requested to summon Luo Yanfu to court to investigate and recover the debt. The defendant, Luo Yanfu, also hired a lawyer to represent him, stating that the defendant had left town for business and would not return to Shanghai for about two months. He requested an adjournment for further trial. Judge Gong approved the request for a seven-day postponement and ordered the defendant to appear in court in person for further investigation.

Man Jumps into the River and is Rescued 126

The Reason for the Suicide Attempt is Not Yet Clear

The Kunshan Maru, a feeder ship of the Japanese-owned Osaka Company, was sailing from the Guangdong Road pier back to the Osaka pier in Pudong at 1 p.m. yesterday when a middle-aged man among the passengers suddenly jumped into the river unnoticed near the fish market pier in the Sixteenth Ward. The captain immediately noticed and stopped the engine to try to rescue him. Fortunately, he was rescued. Because he had swallowed a lot of water and was barely breathing, he was sent by sailors to the Water Police Station and then rushed to Renji Hospital for treatment. After he is no longer in danger, he will be taken back to the police station for questioning. Therefore, his name, age, and reason for suicide are not yet clear.

Male Corpse at the Toyo Company Pier 127

At 9 a.m. yesterday, an unidentified male corpse suddenly floated up on the river surface at the Toyo Company Pier in Hongkou. He was about 30 years old, wearing a gray cotton robe, barefoot, and had very short hair on top of his head. A Chinese policeman on the shore spotted it, reported it to the Hongkou Police Station, and telegraphed the Water Police Station to send a Sampan No. 890 to retrieve the corpse and send it to the Life Saving Bureau for photographs and collection, pending identification.

It is expected that all sectors of Shanghai will not easily let go of this great opportunity.

Tenants of Fengyuli Organize a Tenant Union 129

Meeting Held Yesterday

Four Cases Discussed

All tenants of Fengyuli, Sapo Sai Road, French Concession, opposed the landlord's coercion to sign harsh contracts and held their first preparatory meeting at Lisheng Middle School in Xichengli at 4 p.m. yesterday. More than 30 tenant representatives attended. Tong Gongnu was publicly elected as the temporary chairman. A ceremony was held. Commissioner Yu, sent by the Housing Association, attended and guided the meeting. The following matters were reported: (1) The chairman reported on the renaming of the landlord Huifu Company to Dali and the situation of forcing tenants to sign contracts. (2) Tenant representatives Wu Wenlan and Hu Peiru expressed their opinions, stating that the landlord's profit from building houses exceeds the normal rate of one point by as much as three points. The interest rate on houses should not exceed one point at most, and the standard is usually eight percent. Now that the landlord has such a large interest, he is still not satisfied and wants to raise the rent. It seems that we tenants must unite and deal with it together. (3) Tenants reported that the security in the neighborhood is weak, resulting in frequent theft cases. The Sikh police officers do not carry weapons. Even if there are thieves, they can only let them do as they please. This matter is of great importance to the safety of the tenants. In the future, the landlord will be asked to pay attention to the protection of the tenants. (4) Tenants Ye and Deng reported that the landlord had entrusted lawyer Lin to issue a notice to vacate the house on the grounds of rent arrears and requested assistance. Discussion Matters: (1) It was resolved to organize a tenant union and submit it to the higher authorities for filing. (2) Raising funds: each storefront will contribute one silver dollar and additional funds will be contributed voluntarily at any time. (3) Hu Peiru, Wu Wenlan, Ye Qiangya, Xu Ruiyuan, Zhang Songrong, Fang Jiafen, Tong Gongnu, Huang Laotai and other nine people were elected as secretaries. (4) All application procedures will be handled separately by each preparation member. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

A memorial service was held at the Puyi Agency in the previous month. Because Mr. Han's ancestral home is in the ancient Yue region, he requested leave yesterday to escort the coffin back to his hometown for burial. At 3 p.m., the funeral procession departed from Fuxu Road in Shanghai to the North Railway Station to board the Shanghai-Hangzhou train. When the coffin passed the entrance of the Special District Court on North Zhejiang Road, the Special District Local Court and the Higher Branch Court jointly set up a memorial service. Onlookers blocked the road. The presidents and chief prosecutors of the two courts, all judges, prosecutors, clerks, section chiefs, section members, etc., wore yellow flowers on their lapels and participated in the memorial service and respectfully escorted the plain carriage and white horses. It was truly a grand occasion.

Self-Government and the Provisional Constitution by Pan Gongzhan 139

A Record of a Speech Delivered at the Shanghai Municipal Local Self-Government Training Institute on March 10th of the 20th Year.

Gentlemen, the topic of my speech today is called Self-Government and the Provisional Constitution. I want to briefly explain the relationship between the Provisional Constitution and self-government during the period of political tutelage. Before I begin, let me first roughly describe what the existing Provisional Constitutions of the Republic of China and the Provisional Constitution advocated by the Kuomintang's leader Sun Yat-sen were all about. We know that the Republic of China did have a Provisional Constitution, namely the Provisional Constitution of the first year of the Republic (1912). After the Second Revolution, Yuan Shikai, preparing to become emperor, dissolved the National Assembly and abolished the Provisional Constitution. At this time, our party leader reorganized the Kuomintang into the Chinese Revolutionary Party, preparing to fight again for our principles and for the Republic of China. We coordinated in the Southwest to oppose Yuan Shikai's attempt to become emperor. Yuan Shikai ultimately failed. This revolutionary war can be said to be the National Protection War or the War to Defend the Constitution. The meaning of defending the Constitution is to maintain the Provisional Constitution. After Yuan's death, Li Yuanhong succeeded him as President and ordered the convening of the National Assembly to abide by the Provisional Constitution. However, not long after, in the sixth year of the Republic (1917), Zhang Xun plotted to restore the monarchy and forced him to dissolve the National Assembly again. At that time, Mr. Wu Tingfang and others came to the South to follow Sun Yat-sen in convening an extraordinary National Assembly in Guangzhou to engage in the constitutional protection movement. Later, Wu Peifu of the North turned against the government, and Li Yuanhong reconvened the Sixth National Assembly of the Republic, with Cao Kun bribing his way to the presidency and promulgating a constitution on October 10th of the twelfth year of the Republic (1923), which we call the "Cao Kun Constitution." There were many twists and turns in between. Why do I report this segment of history? It is to make you understand that the Provisional Constitution and the Constitution have both existed in the history of the Republic of China. However, whether the Provisional Constitution and the Constitution are effective depends entirely on whether the people are law-abiding. If there are no law-abiding people, even if there is a Provisional Constitution or a Constitution, it is just a piece of paper and will not be effective. Therefore, we hope that everyone will act within the scope of the law and not think that everything will be fine with the law. With this concept, I am afraid that we will still inevitably repeat the mistakes of the past. Therefore, I have briefly reported the past history.

Now that the central government wants to formulate a Provisional Constitution when convening the National Assembly, we certainly hope to have a Provisional Constitution and at the same time hope to have law-abiding people. If there are no law-abiding people, we will repeat the mistakes of the past. Now, the Chinese Kuomintang and the National Government have resolved to establish a Provisional Constitution, and Sun Yat-sen has always advocated the rule of law and democracy. When others destroyed the Provisional Constitution, he wanted to defend the Constitution. Although the Second Revolution failed, he had to continue to work hard to achieve the final victory. Now, I will talk about the Kuomintang's repeated propositions on the Provisional Constitution. The First National Congress was convened by Sun Yat-sen himself when he was alive. The manifesto of the congress is the crystallization of the congress. The manifesto of the First National Congress criticized the four schools of thought on national salvation at that time. The first was the constitutional monarchists, who advocated that as long as there is a Constitution, China can be saved. Therefore, there is a paragraph in the manifesto: "...Since the first year of the Republic, there has been a Constitution, but the remnants of autocracy, warlords, and bureaucrats have usurped power and committed all kinds of evils..." This refers to the Cao Kun clique. There are also "...Unless these people are removed, the Constitution will not take effect..." This means that warlords and bureaucrats like Cao Kun used the Constitution to usurp positions. Little do they know that if there is a Constitution but no law-abiding people, the Constitution is also useless. Therefore, the manifesto of the First National Congress clearly stated that the constitutionalist proposition cannot save the country. The second is the provincial autonomy faction. This faction was at its peak in the eighth and ninth years of the Republic (1919-1920). They argued that China is too big, so it is better for the provinces to become autonomous. However, the manifesto of the First National Congress pointed out that the proposition of this faction is not really to save the country but that a small number of warlords want to use this pretext to carve up territories. The figures of this faction include Chen Jiongming, Tang Jiyao, and Zhao Hengti. Sun Yat-sen did not oppose autonomy. Autonomy must be discussed after the country is truly unified. The period of political tutelage is to start from local autonomy. Only when the people have the ability to govern themselves can the Provisional Constitution and the Constitution be guaranteed. The period of political tutelage is the period of implementing local autonomy, which naturally has to be after the revolutionary army has settled down.

Speaking of this point, the Kuomintang should have completed the Northern Expedition long ago from the Northern Expedition in the fifteenth year of the Republic (1926) to the Northern Expedition in the twentieth year of the Republic (1931). However, for the past four or five years since the seventeenth, eighteenth, and nineteenth years of the Republic (1928-1930), warlords have successively stirred up trouble, and construction has not been able to progress. For the past four or five years, the central government has been working hard to suppress the rebels. Until last year, the Yan-Feng reactionary group was formed. This was the final battle between the Kuomintang and the reactionaries. Although the final goal of the revolution has not been achieved, the National Revolution has also achieved considerable victories. Its environment should be different from the past. At this time, if the Kuomintang does not talk about the Provisional Constitution, does not do local self-government work, and does not work hard on political tutelage and construction, then the Kuomintang has become a liar. In the period of military administration, military law is used. After the revolutionary army unifies the country, it is the period of political tutelage. Military law is naturally not applicable. The period of political tutelage is to talk about the law. Of course, a Provisional Constitution is needed. Several comrades in the central government want to discuss the Provisional Constitution when convening the National Assembly. This kind of Provisional Constitution is the Provisional Constitution of the period of political tutelage, and it is also the Provisional Constitution that should be jointly observed by the whole country during the period of political tutelage. The manifesto of the First National Congress pointed out that the constitutional monarchists are liars, and the provincial autonomy faction is also liars. The Kuomintang, in view of the mistakes of the past, advocated that after the period of military administration, there should be a Provisional Constitution in the period of political tutelage. Although the Outline of National Reconstruction has only twenty-five articles, it clearly stipulates the work of the three periods of military administration, political tutelage, and constitutional government. Whenever a province or county is within the reach of the National Government, it is the beginning of political tutelage. Furthermore, in the manifesto of the Tongmenghui (1905), even before the Republic of China, in addition to the four principles in the manifesto, there were three periods: (1) the rule of military law (i.e., the period of military administration), (2) the rule of the Provisional Constitution (the period of political tutelage), and (3) the rule of the Constitution (the period of constitutional government). It can be seen that the division of the three periods of military administration, political tutelage, and constitutional government was decided as early as the Tongmenghui era. Furthermore, in the sixth chapter of Sun Yat-sen's teachings, there is a paragraph: "...The period of revolutionary progress is divided into three: first, the period of military administration, second, the period of political tutelage, and third, the period of constitutional government..." Below is an explanation: "The second is the period of destruction. It is planned to implement military law during this period, with the revolutionary army taking on the responsibility of breaking the autocracy of the Qing Dynasty, eliminating the corruption of the bureaucracy, reforming the bad habits of customs, relieving the inequality of slaves, washing away the flow of opium, destroying the superstition of feng shui, and removing the obstacles of likin, etc..." The work of the period of military administration is to use military force to eliminate bureaucrats and warlords, as well as to wash away the opium scourge and likin. However, opium has not been eradicated to this day. If during the period of military administration, those who plant opium, sell opium, and use opium were punished by military law, there would be no opium at this time. However, this kind of work was not done during the period of military administration. Now, during the period of political tutelage, it is more difficult to do this kind of work. For example, the abolition of likin was also done during the period of military administration. It was not until January 1, 1931, that likin was abolished throughout the country. These are all due to the failure to do the work of the period of military administration during the period of military administration. The second is the transition period. The meaning of transition is the middle between the period of destruction and the period of construction, which is called the transition period. Below is an explanation: "...It is planned to implement the Provisional Constitution (not the current one) during this period, build local autonomy, and promote the development of civil rights, with a county as the unit of autonomy, and the county further divided into rural areas..." This paragraph has the four words "not the current one." Its meaning refers to the so-called Provisional Constitution, not the then-current Provisional Constitution. It can be seen that Sun Yat-sen's proposition has always been consistent, that is, during the period of political tutelage, there should be a Provisional Constitution that builds local autonomy and promotes the development of civil rights. Although the Outline of National Reconstruction has only a few articles, its spirit is focused on local autonomy. As for the beginning of the period of political tutelage, Article 7 of the Outline of National Reconstruction clearly stipulates that "the day when a province is completely settled is the time when political tutelage begins, and the day when military administration ceases." For example, when the National Revolutionary Army arrives in Zhejiang and then from Zhejiang to Jiangsu, the military affairs of Zhejiang are considered settled, which is the beginning of the period of political tutelage. Articles 9, 10, 11, 12, 13, and 14 of the Outline of National Reconstruction all focus on local autonomy and the new work of local autonomy, such as investigating the population, surveying land, organizing police affairs, improving sanitation, expanding education, and building roads, etc. The processing time is tentatively set at three years. If the above matters are handled well within three years, the people can elect the county magistrate. If the above matters can be handled well in less than three years, the county magistrate can also be elected by the people. If every county in a province can do this, it is the beginning of the period of constitutional government, and the provincial governor can also be elected by the people. The autonomy advocated by Sun Yat-sen starts from the lower level, not like Cao Kun, Chen Jiongming, and others who hang up the signboard of law or autonomy and use it as their tool. If more than half of the provinces in the country have provincial governors elected by the people and have completed local autonomy, then a National Assembly can be convened at this time (which is different in nature from the National Conference to be convened now) to determine the Constitution and promulgate it. The day the Constitution is promulgated is the completion of constitutional government. At that time, the National Government is completely an elected government. It can be seen that the Provisional Constitution of the period of political tutelage is the law that everyone jointly observes during the period of political tutelage. Its nature is different from that of the Constitution. See Article 22 of the Outline of National Reconstruction: "The draft Constitution should be based on the achievements of the Outline of National Reconstruction and the two periods of political tutelage and constitutional government, and should be discussed by the Legislative Yuan and publicized to the public at any time for selection and implementation at that time." It can be seen that the Constitution should refer to the achievements of the two periods and be drafted by the Legislative Yuan, and then submitted to the National Assembly for a vote and promulgated it. Therefore, the Provisional Constitution and the Constitution are fundamentally different.

Sun Yat-sen especially paid attention to striving for local autonomy during the period of political tutelage. Therefore, for the work done in local autonomy, the Local Autonomy Beginning Implementation Law, such as clearing the population, establishing institutions, setting land prices, building roads, reclaiming wasteland, establishing schools, is stipulated in detail. In the future, when formulating the Provisional Constitution, we must infuse this spirit into it, so that it will not be empty. During the period of political tutelage, the Kuomintang wants to enable the people to receive training in exercising the four powers. The National Conference is an opportunity for the government and the people to cooperate. The meaning of the two words "Provisional Constitution" is the public agreement between the people and the government. In other words, it is everyone's joint contract. If the Provisional Constitution stipulates 100 articles, everyone must jointly abide by these 100 articles of the contract. Formulating the Provisional Constitution is to summarize all of Sun Yat-sen's teachings, consider the needs of the times, and abide by the guidelines of political tutelage, and write a few articles neatly so that everyone can jointly abide by them during the period of political tutelage. This law, whether it is for party members or non-party members, the government and the people must abide by it. The meaning of setting the Provisional Constitution is that Chairman Chiang and Committee Member Dai Jitao have made it very clear at the central memorial week, that it is to set the Provisional Constitution for the permanent peace, unification, and construction of the country. Therefore, if the Provisional Constitution does not pay attention to the cultivation of local autonomy and the purpose of completing unification and construction, it will not be able to achieve the Provisional Constitution. If the Provisional Constitution only pays attention to the provisions of the presidential system, cabinet system, council system, and bicameral system, and ignores the scope of work of the period of political tutelage stipulated in the Outline of National Reconstruction, in other words, ignores local autonomy, then the Provisional Constitution in the future may be equal to the Provisional Constitution of the first year of the Republic, and not the Provisional Constitution that Sun Yat-sen hoped for.

If someone wants to ask why we need to formulate the Provisional Constitution when we already have Sun Yat-sen's teachings, in fact, formulating the Provisional Constitution is for the people to easily understand Sun Yat-sen's teachings and to facilitate joint compliance. Therefore, formulating the Provisional Constitution, on the one hand, cannot violate Sun Yat-sen's teachings, and on the other hand, it must train the general public to thoroughly comply with the Provisional Constitution from top to bottom. If there is a law, but there are no law-abiding people, this law is still useless. To have law-abiding people, we must cultivate local self-government talents. If you understand this point, you should know that your own responsibilities are very important. After you graduate from this research here, there is still a lot of work to be done in the future. Don't think that these three months are for learning, and you don't have to learn outside. You are learning outside all the time, and these learnings are still real learnings. What you are learning now is just learning the articles of the local autonomy regulations and the items of the local autonomy cause. Therefore, the real learning is to learn in society. The responsibilities you bear are very heavy. I hope you will work hard. (End)

World Snippets 140

— Hai Ke

▲In Carlisle, a city in the Cumberland region of England, a large mirror is placed at every dangerous intersection to prevent accidents. However, women who drive their own cars often use them as vanity mirrors, taking a moment to primp and pose.

▲In southern France, countless termites have suddenly appeared, causing extensive damage to crops. They have also been found in Paris, where they are wreaking havoc.

▲On the cliffs of Great Orme's Head in Wales, someone discovered over a thousand pigeon feet around an eagle's nest. Most of them were fitted with rings. Apparently, they were homing pigeons that were caught by the eagle while flying and brought back to be eaten.

▲In Kansas, USA, anyone who sells or gives away cigarettes or cigarette rolling paper is considered to have committed an illegal act and is subject to prosecution.

▲The British and Foreign Bible Society prints and distributes the Bible around the world in over 558 languages, enabling people of all nations and regions to read it.

▲A Scottish mining engineer discovered the ruins of an ancient city in Mexico. The remaining buildings are still visible. It is estimated to be at least 4,000 years old.

A Record of the Four Caves on South Hill, West Lake 141

— Bao Xing

I previously read in "Free Talk" about the scenic spots of the Four Caves, such as Ziyun Cave, but they were all along the North Hill route. The Four Caves on South Hill were not mentioned at all. I am now providing a supplementary account.

Climbing the steps from Yangmei Ridge, one reaches Yanxia Cave. The cave is surrounded by a bamboo fence, providing a place for tourists to rest their sedan chairs. The entrance to the cave is not wide, and the depth is only about ten steps, so the cave is not very dark or damp. The stone walls inside the cave are carved with hundreds of small Buddha statues, each with a different appearance. However, they are not as vivid or majestic as those carved on Feilai Peak. At the bottom of the cave wall, there is a small hole, only about a foot in diameter, which is unusually dark. When you reach in, you feel a biting cold. If you throw a stone into it, you cannot hear it falling. Some say that this cave leads to Mount Tianmu. Such idle talk is not worth a knowing person's smile.

Turning left from Yanxia Cave and descending, passing a pavilion, one reaches Shuile Cave. The cave has two entrances, one on the left and one on the right. The cold air inside the cave chills one to the bone. Even in the height of summer, it feels like late autumn. A monk has set up tables and chairs to entertain guests and orders a young monk to carry a lantern to guide them to explore the bottom of the cave. The cave is about a hundred or several tens of feet deep and about eight or nine feet wide. It is very damp inside. Water trickles down the stone walls. Even though there is a cement path, it is still muddy and slippery. Walking along the wall for about ten steps, there are stone lotus roots and stone bamboos standing opposite each other, but they do not look very realistic. This is probably not the work of humans. Further in, the width only allows for one person to pass. On the left, there is a stone drum, which makes a sound when struck. The stone bell on the right is only similar in shape and cannot actually make a bell sound. Further in, one cannot hold one's head high and must stoop to walk. The sound of water gurgles underfoot, making it eerie and frightening. Just as one reaches the bottom of the cave, one sees a torrent of cold spring water rushing down, which is truly spectacular. There is also a small hole at the bottom of the cave. The monk said that it could still be opened up, but the project would be huge.

Climbing up from Shuile Cave, one reaches Shiwu Cave. The temple outside the cave is clean and tidy, the best of the caves. The flowers and trees are lush, and the ponds and stones are elegant, resembling a secluded paradise. It cannot be compared to the desolation of the other caves. The four walls inside the cave are also carved with Buddha statues of varying sizes. The cave is very shallow, so it is still bright. The ground is also not wet. In the center of the cave, there is a square pond. The spring water creates whirlpools, just like Tiger Spring. The monk puts a bowl in the water, saying that if someone can throw money into it, they have a karmic connection with the Buddha. Foolish men and women all scramble to open their purses, so they accumulate at the bottom of the pond. The monk's method of collecting money cannot be said to be clumsy. Next to the cave, there are more than ten stone steps. There is another cave with only four walls, nothing worth seeing. When a stone is thrown into the bottom of the cave, there is a rushing sound, which is the downstream of the pond spring.

Walking up the mountain from the back door of the Shiwu Cave temple, one soon sees a small cave appearing in the rugged rocks, commonly known as the Immortal Cave. The entrance to the cave is narrow and unbearable, and one must bow one's head to enter. The cave is only large enough to accommodate a small statue of Emperor Gaozong of the Song Dynasty. The monk said that when the Jin soldiers were chasing Emperor Gaozong during the Southern Crossing, the emperor hid in this cave for seven days and nights. Later, he took the throne in Lin'an, thus protecting half of Jiangnan. This is probably just unfounded talk. (Que Chou)

On the Matter of the Scripture-Chanting Beggar Zhu Si 142

— Jun Mei

A peculiar beggar came to our town some time ago. He wandered along the road, chanting the Prajna Paramita Heart Sutra every day to earn a living. People were happy to buy his services because he chanted the sutra earnestly and did not do it casually. When asked about it, the beggar would say, "I committed serious sins in the first half of my life, and I am afraid of falling into hell after death, so I use this to repent. Moreover, when people get my sutra, they also accumulate some merit." My cousin Yuquan, who lives in Jiashan, told me about this beggar in great detail, so I wrote it down.

The beggar's surname is Zhu, and his given name is A Si. He is from Jiashan, Zhejiang. His elder brother is the second in his lineage and is a wealthy man in the village. Zhu was extremely poor. Some people urged him to go and live with his elder brother. Zhu would arrogantly reply, "How can that be? Suffering is just a common thing. Do I want to get rich today? My brother is indeed wealthy in the village, but what about after his death?" After saying this, he would act disdainfully and leave. At first, Zhu's family was not poor. He had a fondness for pleasures since he was young. He once took a thousand gold pieces to the sea and wandered among the brothels. He returned after spending all his money, without any complaints. He also said that it was a great joy to spend money on women. If one regards money as one's life, then one is extremely foolish. When he said this, he would quote Gong Ding'an's line, "I wish to have ten million taels of gold to befriend all the famous scholars and beauties in the world," to boast about himself. His boldness and unruliness were like this. Soon after, he suddenly disappeared. Ten years later, he suddenly returned as a beggar. His face was haggard and his clothes were tattered. He begged along the streets every day and made a living by catching snakes. His skills were excellent and unparalleled. Therefore, the ruffians in the village all took him as their teacher. His name for catching snakes spread throughout Zhejiang. However, the general's chicken may die in battle. Zhu, who was good at catching snakes, ended up losing his sight in a certain mountain in Shaoxing, Zhejiang. At first, his disciples still supported him every year and did not neglect him in the slightest. However, Zhu did not want to live off others, so he left and traveled all over Jiangsu and Zhejiang, repenting by begging and chanting scriptures. He had killed living beings wantonly when he was young, and his sins were so deep that he still hoped to lay down the butcher's knife and become a Buddha immediately. The beggar Zhu is worthy of praise. Therefore, I wrote down his story to satirize the world.

An Examination of Ancient Women's Adornments 143

— Qian Fu

▲I once traveled to Tianjin and Shanghai and jokingly discussed stories of ancient women's adornments with two or three close friends. However, as the ancient times are far away, their meanings are gradually blurred. Listening to the rain by the banana window, sitting idly and bored, I jotted them down haphazardly.

▲The pei is a type of skirt. In "Miscellaneous Records of Women's Needlework," Yan Zhao Wang bestowed on Xuan Juan a mountain poem: "Lowering her head, she sees her slanted hair, dragging clouds and playing with a slender pei."

▲The ru is a type of jacket. In the ancient poem "Shang Sang," "Yellow silk is the lower skirt, purple silk is the upper ru." In Yu Ji's poem, "For no reason, a pair of butterflies fly onto the purple silk ru."

▲The jue are shoes. The palace women of Emperor Donghun of Qi all wore green silk jue.

▲The zan is used to hold up hair. In ancient times, men had full hair, so men also used them. In Li Shanfu's poem "Poor Woman," "In her life, she has never known embroidered clothes, but she secretly grieves while holding a thorn hairpin."

▲The dian is a golden head ornament. In Liu Xiaowei's "Lotus Picking Song," "Dewdrops sometimes wet the bracelet, and wind stalks lightly brush the dian."

▲The chai is a forked hairpin for women. In Liang Huang's "Sleeping Beauty in Spring Poem," "A fallen hairpin still hangs in her sideburns, and light sweat wants to melt the yellow."

▲The sheng is a head ornament. During the Han Dynasty, it was called Hua Sheng.

▲The tiaotuo is a bracelet. There are two types, gold and jade. In "Complete Tang Poetry Anecdotes," Emperor Xuanzong once composed a poem, with the line "golden buyao" but could not find a matching line. Wen Tingjun's talent and beauty filled the line "jade tiaotuo" after it. Emperor Xuanzong appreciated it. Su Shi's "Crisp Cake Poem" says, "Last night's spring sleep was stronger than wine, pressing down on the beautiful woman's wrapped gold arm," note: This is the gold tiaotuo.

▲The buyao is a crown ornament for empresses. In "Seven Edicts," "Wearing the glittering golden buyao, waving the paired jade quills."

Rise Late in Life 144

— Qiu Shui

A person's childhood is the developmental age, middle age is the educational age, and old age is the rising age. Therefore, the success of a great man's career often comes after the age of fifty. Conversely, a person who achieves success in his youth often does not last long. This claim is not nonsense on my part. Not only is there evidence to prove it, but it can also be inferred by ordinary people. Because middle age is still the preparatory age, and rising to prominence in middle age is often due to chance. The foundation is not solid, and collapse is a concern. What do you think, right or wrong?

The Secretary-General of the British Parliament is a good position, a transitional stage for promoting ministers. All the famous ministers of the United Kingdom have come from the Secretary-General. This also shows the superiority of the Secretary-General's position. The most recent person to hold this position is Frank Smith. He only took this position last year and is 76 years old. His superior, George Lansbury, is also someone who rose to prominence late in life. Although he once entered Parliament as a member in 1910, he was not appointed to an important government position until he was 70 years old. In addition, the current British Minister of Aviation, the Duke of Ambery, also appeared on the political stage as late as the age of 70. It can also be seen that life at seventy is not old, and it is not empty talk to say that one is stronger in old age.

The matter of rising late in life is not only found in the political world, but also in various other careers. There was an old man in Sweden named Han Erfansheng. He recently died at the age of 102. Most of his life's work was spent on farming. When he grew older and his arm strength gradually weakened, his spirit remained the same. He abandoned farming and engaged in fishing and hunting. He did not discourage himself because of his old age and relearned the art of shooting. A year before his death, he also won the championship in a shooting competition in Sweden.

Jiang Taigong met King Wen at the age of eighty. His great career was all achieved above the age of eighty. Therefore, a person's failure in his youth is not worth worrying about, and one should not be discouraged by old age and weakness. I deeply hope that those who read my article will think deeply about it.

Advocating Shuttlecock Kicking 145

— Li Bing

The customs of our country vary from place to place, but the game of kicking shuttlecock is popular in both the north and the south. Its origins are quite ancient and, like swinging on a swing, it is a beneficial exercise. In previous years, Mr. Chu Minyi of my hometown vigorously advocated kicking shuttlecock, saying that this game involves the movement of all parts of the body. The eyes, hands, and feet are all connected. It is truly an excellent method to promote health and develop physical strength. His words are good and are welcomed by those who care about sports. The method of kicking shuttlecock varies slightly across the country. In my hometown, it is customary to take advantage of the cold winter and spring weather to ward off the cold. As for the innovative patterns, there are various names such as sweeping, jumping, lifting, and circling. Generally, the names differ depending on the kicking method. Judging by its classification, there are no less than dozens of items. However, in my hometown, the loser is only fined one chip. In the competitions in Fujian Province, sweets and peanuts are used as prizes. This probably increases the interest of both parties, but it is rare to see money used for winning or losing.

According to a friend, the Manchus also liked the game of kicking shuttlecock after entering the Central Plains. On good days in early spring, both young and old would gather. The shuttlecocks were made with particular care, with feathers attached to them. They were generally divided into red, black, yellow, and white, and of various weights and lengths, each according to their preference. This can be said to be a particularly elaborate study. The experts in this art in Beijing can not only kick with both feet, but also kick with the top of their heads without looking back, and without the shuttlecock falling to the ground. The skill and proficiency is not easy to achieve without years of effort.

Shuttlecock was also popular in Europe in ancient times. In the heyday of Rome, the common people quite liked it. However, the shuttlecocks used long feathers and were relatively large. One must choose an opponent to pass it back and forth. The patterns used by the feet were simpler than those of the habitually practicing in our country. Later, with the rise of tennis, its method was based on kicking shuttlecock. Therefore, after the fourteenth century, shuttlecock fell behind, and tennis gradually became an important sport. The English name for shuttlecock is Shuttle Cock. It can be seen that England also had this game in ancient times. The above was said by Mr. Shen. Shen studied in England in the past, so it seems to be not without basis.

Travelogue of India (15) 146

— Linghua

3rd. Mr. Sita took me to visit the Victoria Memorial Palace. We departed from the university by car. Each person paid two annas. Upon arrival, we entered through the north gate. There were lion statues on both sides. At the main gate, two bronze cannons were displayed. Patrols in red caps and leather belts guarded the place like a royal ceremony. Once inside, there were many patrols, as if it were a forbidden palace. Below, various oil paintings were displayed, all portraits of Queen Victoria. On the upper level, in the inner sections, were portraits of her husband, Albert, and son, Edward. There were portraits of Queen Victoria at her coronation and baptism, various portraits from her youth to old age, portraits of her on horseback, portraits of her writing letters, and the last letter she sent to India. Observing her attire in full dress, the train was very long, requiring someone to drag it from behind. Previously, I had seen in movies that the trains of Western women's court dresses could be as long as twenty feet. The attire of Chinese imperial consorts and their phoenix robes were all imitations of the beauty of birds' long tails. This is perhaps a universal principle of aesthetics, and proof that one person is not as naturally beautiful as a bird. I think long tails are rare to be longer than twenty feet. Their dignity is also comparable to that of noble concubines in the human world.

The dome of this palace is extremely solemn, reminding one of the Empress Dowager Cixi of the Summer Palace in Beijing. On the upper level, there are red-bearded patrols everywhere, as if facing an enemy. However, the displays are all landscapes and houses from various parts of India. There are also British artillery forts and scenes of soldiers and cannons drilling. There is a view of the Himalayas, with many Western-style houses on the mountains, used for escaping the heat of India. There are many incense burners displayed in various places, seemingly for burning incense, and many Indian men and women come to see them, reminding one of the imperial incense burners in the three main halls of Beiping. At the very top level is a dome, which is about twenty to thirty feet high and seems unattainable. It is entirely filled with various colorful portraits of the Queen, looking down at the central hall on the lower level. There is also a statue of the Queen. The south gate displays large and short cannons, two of which were seized from the French. Besides the Queen, there are many statues of military generals, civil officials, and female officials. The construction of this palace largely uses marble. When asked, the Indians said that this stone comes from North India and takes four or five days by train to arrive. The third level displays state documents and official papers, various British and Indian texts and seals, related to court matters. It is also interspersed with Indian customs and various scenes. This is the method of Westerners, to compare everything in the exhibition hall, showing the shortcomings of others by showing their own strengths, making people feel ashamed, admire, and surrender to the greatness of their politics, education, and art. Is this not great? We shall see in the future.

There are many plants in India. Entering the vegetable market, I recognize very few. The trees are tall and provide dense shade, which is better than being inside a room. There is no sunlight, and it is cool, so Indians like to lie on the ground, which is like paradise. We also like to sit under the trees when we come here. Therefore, the Buddha's teaching of sitting under a tree is a custom. Lying on the ground is also a teaching of the Buddha. Even today, Indians everywhere still like to lie on the ground. I have seen this everywhere in Singapore. At first, I thought it was strange, but now I know it is their custom. Pomegranates are very beautiful, similar to peaches and pears in China. Chili peppers are prevalent. Onions are especially common. Chili peppers are called "chili," which is what is meant by "eating chili rice." Indians do not pronounce it "kali," but "chili." The people of Ceylon especially like to eat cinnamon bark, which they consider a common food. I cannot bear it. Banana leaves are as large as mats and are used to wrap things. Walnuts are white and very large, similar to those in China. Sugar production is significant. There are sugar food and snack shops everywhere, which are quite delicious. The strange thing is that there are very few restaurants. This is very inconvenient for guests.

Educational News and Important Information

Ministry of Education Investigates the Status of Students Studying Abroad 147

The Ministry of Education, in order to investigate the status of returned students and students studying abroad, sent official letters to various domestic and foreign institutions and embassies in Europe and America, stating: "Our country's dispatch of students to study abroad was originally intended to reserve specialized talents for construction, which is of great importance to the country's future. At this initial stage of political tutelage, there is an urgent need for talent. Whether the returned students from the past can meet the demand, and how the standards for future dispatch should be determined, must first be carefully investigated to have a basis. Therefore, the Ministry has formulated two types of survey forms: A. Survey form on the current service status of returned students in the country (such as the current service institution, the position held, the monthly salary, whether they have joined the party, the year of going abroad, whether they are self-funded or government-funded, which school they graduated from in the country, which country and school they graduated from, which subjects they studied, the degree obtained, experience, future plans, etc.); B. Survey form on students currently studying in various countries (such as the country of study, the subjects studied, the grade level, the current position of those who have not returned to the country after graduation, whether they are self-funded or government-funded, the various study expenses abroad, whether they have joined the party, etc.). The domestic and foreign students will be investigated simultaneously to compile statistics. In addition to being distributed, the corresponding forms are enclosed, and you are requested to fill them out and return them, and forward them to be filled out and sent directly to the Ministry for statistics."

Beijing Municipal Education Urgently Needs Relief 148

Document Submitted by the Ministry of Education to the Executive Yuan

The Ministry of Education submitted a document to the Executive Yuan stating: "According to the instructions of the Executive Yuan, after the provincial and municipal governments submit administrative plans to the Yuan on a quarterly basis, they should first be submitted to the ministries and commissions for review within their respective areas of responsibility. This has been notified and implemented. Now, the Nanjing Municipal Government has submitted the administrative plan for January to March of the 20th year to the Yuan. In addition to being distributed, the original plan is enclosed for your Ministry to review in detail within its area of responsibility and report back to the Yuan for review. Regarding the educational aspects of this plan, there are no major issues regarding social education, but regarding school education, the plans for the second semester and class levels seem to fail to consider the actual needs. The capital's education is related to the views of both domestic and foreign observers. The number of school-age children in the city who are out of school is around 30,000 and urgently needs relief. It is proposed that the Executive Yuan order the Nanjing Municipal Government to pay close attention to educational administration and designate a certain percentage of the subsidies allocated by the Executive Yuan specifically for the promotion of elementary education. Please also order the Nanjing Municipal Education Bureau to submit a special report to the Ministry for review on the progress of the promotion of elementary education in the past two and a half months. Whether this is appropriate is hereby submitted with the original plan for your review and implementation."

Jiangsu Province's Measures for Rewarding and Punishing Literacy Movement in Various Counties 149

The Jiangsu Provincial Literacy Movement Propaganda Committee formulated the following measures for rewarding and punishing the literacy movement in various counties of Jiangsu Province:

Article 1: The Jiangsu Provincial Literacy Movement Propaganda Committee hereby formulates these measures to assess the achievements of the literacy movement in various counties of the province.

Article 2: These measures apply to the following personnel: 1. Chairman and Vice-Chairman of the County Committee; 2. Chairman of the District Sub-Committee; 3. Chairman of the Township Branch Committee.

Article 3: Counties that have the following facts in the literacy movement will be rewarded: 1. Those who earnestly implement the various laws and regulations of the Committee and the province for the literacy movement; 2. Those who establish and improve the various literacy movement organizations that should be established and work hard; 3. Those who hold literacy movement propaganda weeks on schedule and achieve effective results; 4. Those who can promote the establishment of literacy venues for the public after holding propaganda weeks; 5. Those who have other special achievements.

Article 4: Rewards are divided into the following categories according to the level of achievement: 1. Commendation; 2. Merit; 3. Major Merit; 4. Special Recognition.

Article 5: Counties that have the following facts in the literacy movement will be punished: 1. Those who violate the various laws and regulations of the Committee and the province for the literacy movement or fail to implement them effectively; 2. Those who delay in organizing the various literacy movement organizations that should be established or whose organizations are not sound, thereby hindering the progress of the work; 3. Those who do not hold literacy movement propaganda weeks on schedule or whose propaganda is inappropriate and perfunctory; 4. Those who do not promote the establishment of literacy venues for the public after holding propaganda weeks; 5. Those who have other circumstances of failure to perform their duties.

Article 6: Punishments are divided into the following categories according to the severity of the circumstances: 1. Admonition; 2. Demerit; 3. Major Demerit; 4. Salary Deduction.

Article 7: The rewards and punishments stipulated in these measures shall be submitted by the Committee to the provincial government for referral to the relevant competent authorities for separate implementation.

Article 8: These measures shall be implemented after being resolved by the Jiangsu Provincial Literacy Movement Propaganda Committee and approved by the provincial government.

Since its establishment, the Jiangsu Provincial Capital's Experimental Education Zone, affiliated with the Provincial Department of Education, has had its internal staff actively working. Central Film and Cultural Propaganda Committee (Continued) 151

(4) Propaganda of Culture: Culture is one of the three essential elements of establishing a country, and it should be promoted and expanded. It is clear that those in our country who study the West often have the problem of learning its superficial aspects without learning its spirit. Because of this, they despise the culture of their motherland and excessively worship foreigners. Foreign countries take advantage of this mentality to carry out their cultural aggression. Moreover, foreigners in general are almost completely ignorant of our country's culture. When they see yellow-skinned people with polite manners and neatly dressed men and women, they say they are Japanese. Beautiful Chinese goods are said to be Japanese goods. Those who have traveled to Europe and America can attest to this. Furthermore, there is a word in the French dictionary, Chinoiserie, which means cursing someone for being unclean. From this, it can be seen that the dignity of culture has such a close relationship with international status and national superiority. Can we not make every effort to promote it? The magnificence of our country's ancient capital, the Forbidden City, the grandeur of the imperial tombs and temples, the solemnity of various temples and monasteries, the greatness of the Great Wall and the Grand Canal, the exquisite craftsmanship of porcelain and art, the richness of the Siku Quanshu, and the simple folk customs of the inland all sufficiently demonstrate a long-standing and beautiful culture that can inspire admiration in foreigners. If systematic Chinese travel and visit films and historical films are made and screened in foreign countries, what would their public opinion and impact be like in a few years compared to today? On the contrary, the films made by foreigners, concerning inhuman acts, and the performances of adultery, theft, and slavery, are all performed by Chinese people. Their implied meaning is to make the general audience regard the Chinese nation as the world's earliest, most dirty, and culture-lacking nation, so that their countrymen can unite their efforts to eliminate this culture-lacking nation. Their intentions are extremely profound. All those who have traveled to foreign countries, upon seeing this, cannot help but feel heartbroken. In recent years, the study of film has become increasingly prosperous, and the Japanese have taken advantage of it to introduce various scientific inventions from Europe and America for reference. Therefore, their cultural progress has also been rapidly promoted. It can be seen that the relationship between the film industry and culture is important, and we must catch up urgently.

(5) Propaganda of Education: The foundation of a country lies in education. Film can especially supplement the shortcomings of education. Its function can transform social customs and improve public thought. For example, the League of Nations has specially established a film department to regulate the plots of films in various countries. Its intention is to prevent the incitement of people and specially produce films about the tyrannical behavior of the aristocracy during the imperial era to highlight the needs of their red ideology and to concentrate national thought. As for other films that use film to explore the North Pole, report on African news, travel notes, etc., to serve as political and scientific references, they are even more numerous. In medicine, such as the metamorphosis of microorganisms and the anatomy of the human body, etc.; in history, such as the great achievements of ancient heroes, the words and deeds of philosophers, etc.; in geography, such as the topography of mountains and rivers, the customs of various places, etc.; in the military, such as shooting training, the arrangement of the rear, etc.; in natural science, such as the extent of nature and inventions, etc.; in law, such as court trials of criminals and the circumstances of their trials, etc., all can supplement the shortcomings of education and increase the common sense of the public. Its extensive function can be called the most effective tool of propaganda, and nothing can surpass it. Today, our country's school education is neither common nor well-equipped, and social education is even more lacking. Regardless of international etiquette, even public morality and personal conduct are not emphasized. If we use films to demonstrate the actual conditions of social education in various countries, as well as the management of municipal, rural, and factory schools, etc., the benefits to our country's educational future would be boundless. The Western films we see today that describe their country's wealth and depict their licentiousness and extravagance are extremely harmful. How can we speak of benefits?

(6) Propaganda of Hygiene: The peace and tranquility of a country lies in the perfection of the country's organization, and the happiness of a person depends on the soundness of their body and mind. Unfortunately, our people are known as the "sick men of East Asia," which is extremely shameful. However, it is a fact that the majority of the people are physically and mentally unhealthy. This is all due to a lack of hygiene. Although the government has made every effort to promote new hygienic policies, the effect has not been great. Why is this? It is because of ingrained habits. If we look at the alleys and streets, they are filled with filth and garbage, all emitting foul odors that are unbearable. Even if we enforce the law, they still do not change or improve, because the public has no common sense of hygiene. Death and disease are what people fear, and strength and health are what people enjoy. However, why do they not know how to follow this path? It is because of a lack of propaganda. Now, if we use film to show the causes of disease and the rampant spread of germs, as well as the methods of strengthening the body and prolonging life, the public can gain a considerable amount of common sense. If the government supervises them from behind, not only will the nation become stronger day by day, but the habit of hygiene will be cultivated, and foreigners will also respect us. The increase in the nation's status is just the beginning. (To be continued)

Fudan University Invites Wang Zhaocheng to Give a Lecture 154

In particular, the research on "Viyel Cream," a vitamin product produced by the company, was fully elaborated.
